<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_80233c3c-0736-4a1a-bef7-020038fb26e7'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer965544420246999624">Sixteen-year-old Kyra, a highly-skilled potions master, is the only one who knows her kingdom is on the verge of destruction—which means she’s the only one who can save it. Faced with no other choice, Kyra decides to do what she does best: poison the kingdom’s future ruler, who also happens to be her former best friend.<br/><br/>But, for the first time ever, her poisoned dart . . . </span>
  <span id="freeText965544420246999624" style="display:none">Sixteen-year-old Kyra, a highly-skilled potions master, is the only one who knows her kingdom is on the verge of destruction—which means she’s the only one who can save it. Faced with no other choice, Kyra decides to do what she does best: poison the kingdom’s future ruler, who also happens to be her former best friend.<br /><br />But, for the first time ever, her poisoned dart . . . misses.<br /><br />Now a fugitive instead of a hero, Kyra is caught in a game of hide-and-seek with the king’s army and her potioner ex-boyfriend, Hal. At least she’s not alone. She’s armed with her vital potions, a too-cute pig, and Fred, the charming adventurer she can’t stop thinking about. Kyra is determined to get herself a second chance (at murder), but will she be able to find and defeat the princess before Hal and the army find her?<br /><br />Kyra is not your typical murderer, and she’s certainly no damsel-in-distress—she’s the lovable and quick-witted hero of this romantic novel that has all the right ingredients to make teen girls swoon.</span>

It has a part where she takes off her clothes to cross the river when she meets the guy.   <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_629131648" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/629131648" />
    <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies"><img alt="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1500999223p2/4527753.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/629131648?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies?shelf=to-read-released">to-read-released</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer629131648" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3088690931183856594"><blockquote>
  <i>The princess had to die. It was either her or the rest of the kingdom.</i>
</blockquote>That's great, but <b>
  <i>why?</i>
</b> This book had two major problems: it was a rambling mess, and it had huge, gaping plot holes. Half the times I wasn't sure what's going on, and the other half of the time, and for the majority of the book, I was asking myself: <b>Why the fuck did Kyra have to kill the princess?</b><br/><br/>First off, <b>I know the author died of cancer</b>. It is a horrible, horrible way to die. I am sorry for her loss, I am sure she w</span>
  <span id="freeText3088690931183856594" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>The princess had to die. It was either her or the rest of the kingdom.</i>
</blockquote>That's great, but <b>
  <i>why?</i>
</b> This book had two major problems: it was a rambling mess, and it had huge, gaping plot holes. Half the times I wasn't sure what's going on, and the other half of the time, and for the majority of the book, I was asking myself: <b>Why the fuck did Kyra have to kill the princess?</b><br><br>First off, <b>I know the author died of cancer</b>. It is a horrible, horrible way to die. I am sorry for her loss, I am sure she was a wonderful person, I'm sure she was beloved by her friends and family. <b>This review is a review of the book, and not a criticism of the deceased.</b> I did not like the book without any disrespect to her memory.<br><br>I did not like the book. I expected a fun-filled romp of a fantasy, and what I got was more of a romp through a forest of weeds, without an end in sight. The plot and the action was not well-written. It was confusing, the constant flashbacks only served to confuse the present and the past.<br><br>I didn't find the book funny. It was forced, and it was silly. Kyra had a pig, Rosie. Rosie is a stupid pig. I have no fondness the unnecessary inclusion of small children or animals for the sake of cuteness when <b>the situation does not call for it.</b> An accused murderer on the run? There's a situation during which <b>no small cute pig is necessary.</b><blockquote>
  <i>The pig.<br>It was the most ridiculous thing in the entire world: Kyra, would-be assassin and master potioner, had resorted to hunting down her prey—her best friend the princess—with a piglet.<br>But she had no choice. The princess had to die.</i>
</blockquote>I know the book is supposed to be funny and cute. It wasn't such to me; it was forced. Even the cutesy scenes didn't ring true. The main love interest talking down his fierce pet wolf to get wolfie and piggie to be fwiends? No, thank you.<blockquote>
  <i>“See, Rosie? Langley’s a nice dog. He just wants to be friends. I know he’s big and looks scary, but he’s just a puppy at heart. And, Langley, you’re going to have to be gentle with Rosie, okay?”</i>
</blockquote>Now, <b>the reason why the princess had to die was just stupid.</b> I had endure 3/4th of the book with Kyra going <b>WAAAAAAAAH I HAVE TO KILL THE PRINCESS. I HAVE TO KILL MY BEST BEST FRIEND</b> while wondering <b>"Why the fuck you gotta kill your best friend, gurl?"</b> It was frustrating, to say the least. And when the time came for the explanation of WHY SHE GOTTA KILL THE PRINCESS, the explanation made <b>zero sense</b> to me.<blockquote>
  <i>And then, a few weeks later, Kyra was brought to her knees by the second vision she’d ever had in her life.</i>
</blockquote><b>A vision. A bloody vision.</b> How many visions has she ever had in her life? Two. This being the second of them. And OF COURSE THIS VISION CAN BE TRUSTED, RIGHT? What the eff, man?! <b>There's no convincing evidence whatsoever that the princess has to die.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380222758ra/481719.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This was really boring, very forced, overly cutesy, and does not live up to the hype.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3088690931183856594" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_863260232" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/863260232" />
    <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl"><img alt="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603085284p2/8734459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/863260232?book_show_action=true">Feb 23, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽" href="/user/show/8734459-tadiana-night-owl">Tadiana ✩Night Owl☽</a>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/8734459-tadiana-night-owl?shelf=marshmallows-are-less-fluffy">marshmallows-are-less-fluffy</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer863260232" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7424933492190144824"><i>Poison</i> is a cute but rather superficial YA fantasy about Kyra, a 16 year old "potions master" (she seems a little young for master status, but whatever) who's on the run for trying to kill the princess and heir to the throne, for reasons that the author coyly hides from the reader for about half the book. While Kyra's evading arrest, she's also trying to find the princess again so she can do a better job of killing her this time--even though said princess is her best friend. And there's a gorgeo</span>
  <span id="freeText7424933492190144824" style="display:none"><i>Poison</i> is a cute but rather superficial YA fantasy about Kyra, a 16 year old "potions master" (she seems a little young for master status, but whatever) who's on the run for trying to kill the princess and heir to the throne, for reasons that the author coyly hides from the reader for about half the book. While Kyra's evading arrest, she's also trying to find the princess again so she can do a better job of killing her this time--even though said princess is her best friend. And there's a gorgeous (of course) ex-boyfriend helping to hunt Kyra down, as well as a hot (of course) new guy whose path keeps crossing Kyra's.<br><br>The story lags in a few places, the characterization seems a bit lacking, and some of the pieces don't quite fit together the way they should. It's not a terrible book, but it's not deep or challenging in any way. I'd recommend this mostly for younger teen or tween readers who like romantic fantasy. It's worth noting that the MC meets cute guy #2 while she's wading through a river in some frilly underwear. However, there's a small pig with magical man-hunting abilities on top of her head, so there's that.<br><br>It's a very weak 3 stars, but if you love lightweight YA fantasies with clean romance, you might enjoy <i>Poison</i>. For me it was kind of a waste of time.<br><br>On the other hand, now I really want an adorable pink pig that can hunt down anybody I want.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1415863978i/11857106.jpg" width="300" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><i>Go find Richard Armitage for me! NOW!!</i></span>

<div id="review_537898788" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/537898788" />
    <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel"><img alt="♥Rachel♥" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1363996055p2/5481477.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/537898788?book_show_action=true">Feb 16, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="♥Rachel♥" class="user" itemprop="url" name="♥Rachel♥" href="/user/show/5481477-rachel">♥Rachel♥</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer537898788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11490034840370482772"><b>Poison</b> was a fun adventure-fantasy with murder, intrigue, and potions. As if that wasn’t enough, there’s a sweet romance mixed in as well. And don’t forget about the adorable pig. <br/><br/>Kyra, is a Master Potioner who had a bright future ahead of her. She was highly respected in her profession, a mixer of potions that that range from sleeping mixes, truth serums, to extremely lethal poisons. Plus, she was engaged to another brilliant Potioner, Hal. All this was turned upside down when she attempted to </span>
  <span id="freeText11490034840370482772" style="display:none"><b>Poison</b> was a fun adventure-fantasy with murder, intrigue, and potions. As if that wasn’t enough, there’s a sweet romance mixed in as well. And don’t forget about the adorable pig. <br /><br />Kyra, is a Master Potioner who had a bright future ahead of her. She was highly respected in her profession, a mixer of potions that that range from sleeping mixes, truth serums, to extremely lethal poisons. Plus, she was engaged to another brilliant Potioner, Hal. All this was turned upside down when she attempted to kill her best friend, Princess Ariana, the future ruler of her kingdom. Since then she’s been on the run looking for an opportunity to finish the job, otherwise her kingdom will be destroyed. So while dodging discovery by the king’s men, she tries to locate the princess who has now gone into hiding. To find the princess, Kyra enlists the help of a despised criminal Arlo, because she has no other options at this point and time is running out. Enter adorable tracking pig, Rosie. Now armed with her master sniffer Rosie, Kyra goes on the hunt. Along the way she meets the Fred, whom she can’t seem to shake. It doesn’t help matters that Fred is distractingly gorgeous with a “heart-stopping smile.”<br /><br />Oh, this story was just pure fun and adventure! Kyra was strong, capable and a little bit kick-ass. What more could you want in a heroine?! The idea of her wielding potions and having the smarts to make them up was ultra-cool! After being hunted and on the run, she can’t help but be guarded with others, but adorable Rosie and fun-loving Fred slowly creep into her heart, and chip away at her walls: <br /><br /><b>
  <i>Bad enough that she’d gone all soft at the sight of a pig. Now Kyra’s feelings were threatening to overwhelm her because of a few stupid campfire memories, a ghost of a kiss in the night, and the sensation of invisible arms around her in the soft, misty rain.*</i>
</b><br /><br />I thought I knew the story when I picked it up, but new twists and discoveries kept popping up that had me glued to the pages. There was never a dull moment in Poison, and it was easy to breeze right through. Although the romance was not the center of the plot, it was sweet, adorable and enough to satisfy any romance addict. What was a welcome change is that in a sea of YA trilogies, this is a stand-alone and the story wraps up just enough to make you happy. <br /><br />Upon reading the last page I discovered the author, Bridget Zinn passed away, and I had such a sad heart thinking about this. I know she would’ve been a bright addition to YA had she continued writing. <br /><br /><i>*Quotes taken from an uncorrected proof and may change in the final copy. <br /><br />A copy was provided by Disney Hyperion in exchange for an honest review.</i><br /><br />You can find this review and more at <a href="http://thereadersden.blogspot.com/2013/02/review-giveaway-poison-by-bridget-zinn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Readers Den</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11490034840370482772" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_466659141" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/466659141" />
    <a title="Amber Argyle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2254455-amber-argyle"><img alt="Amber Argyle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464712712p2/2254455.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/466659141?book_show_action=true">Nov 29, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber Argyle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber Argyle" href="/user/show/2254455-amber-argyle">Amber Argyle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2254455-amber-argyle?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2254455-amber-argyle?shelf=argyle-book-club">argyle-book-club</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer466659141" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12428644662607194995">Bridget's Zinn's Poison has all the right ingredients to make your heart ache for more.<br/><br/>By raise of hand, who wants an enchanted pig? *waves hand furiously* I'll admit, in the beginning, I was leery about a pig in a high fantasy novel? But the level of cuteness for this pig was off the charts. Also, it was kinda badass. I have no idea how a pig manages all of that, but this one did. Now I want one of my own. <br/><br/>In the beginning, I had a hard time connecting. Great hook. Strong action from the get go</span>
  <span id="freeText12428644662607194995" style="display:none">Bridget's Zinn's Poison has all the right ingredients to make your heart ache for more.<br /><br />By raise of hand, who wants an enchanted pig? *waves hand furiously* I'll admit, in the beginning, I was leery about a pig in a high fantasy novel? But the level of cuteness for this pig was off the charts. Also, it was kinda badass. I have no idea how a pig manages all of that, but this one did. Now I want one of my own. <br /><br />In the beginning, I had a hard time connecting. Great hook. Strong action from the get go, but what kind of story focuses on a main character who killed her best friend and princess? It doesn't take long before we realize that only Kyra knows that the princess has to die or the kingdom does. Murdering the princess will surely cost Kyra her life, but what choice does she have? <br /><br />And then the girl who never misses, missed. Now she has to hide from the king's army, her ex-boyfriend and fellow potioner, witches, and criminals. All while plotting the death of her best friend. <br /><br />Did I mention that there's romance? Cause there is, and I loved it. Poison had the light, sweet kind of romance that tugs a sigh from somewhere deep inside you. <br /><br />I finished the book and tried to find more of Bridget's books so I could immediately buy them. There are none. Bridget died last year. I had to work really hard not to cry. Bridget was a talented new writer with a long and beautiful career before her. I want to hug her. I'll settle for hugging her book and sending my love upwards instead. <br /><br />A must read!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12428644662607194995" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_928442001" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/928442001" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/928442001?book_show_action=true">May 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">People with patience...maybe.</span></div>

          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Cristina Monica by: </span>
      Thank goddness, no one.
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adventure">adventure</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=disappointed">disappointed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=teen-romance">teen-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=do-not-recommend">do-not-recommend</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer928442001" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4486768637247823048">DNF. At 50%.<br/><br/><b>What I wanted and was sure I would say of Poison :</b><br/><br/>''This book…was, of course, not flawless but it had his charms, was enjoyable and made me quite often laugh or smile.'' I can not say that anymore.<br/><br/>At some point, I wasn’t even convinced it really was a young adult book. It just felt so <i>young</i> and childish by moments. And the writing wasn’t impressive or 'rich'. Although, I can’t define it as a middle-grade book because, in of one of the scenes, the MC was in underwear and was being hel</span>
  <span id="freeText4486768637247823048" style="display:none">DNF. At 50%.<br><br><b>What I wanted and was sure I would say of Poison :</b><br><br>''This book…was, of course, not flawless but it had his charms, was enjoyable and made me quite often laugh or smile.'' I can not say that anymore.<br><br>At some point, I wasn’t even convinced it really was a young adult book. It just felt so <i>young</i> and childish by moments. And the writing wasn’t impressive or 'rich'. Although, I can’t define it as a middle-grade book because, in of one of the scenes, the MC was in underwear and was being held by a guy while rescued. But other than that, it’s totally recommended for ten years old readers and plus.<br><br>I think the author did a good job creating an uncommon world with goblins, witches, potion makers, etc. Again, it isn’t as exploited as it could’ve been. The characters sure are unique in their genre and interesting but many of them aren’t as much present for us to get a hold on them.<br><br>This book started actually really good! Kyra, the MC, was searching for something and I could feel her agitation and need to find that ‘thing’. It really woke my curiosity and kept me reading just to know more and find what that ‘thing’ was.<br><br>I also met some new characters but then the action started to slow down. There were some other good scenes afterwards but they either didn’t last long or were completely ridiculous and/or unnecessary. What’s with the witch not being able to enslave Kyra and Fred (friend in that scene) because they tricked the witch by saying they were married? I really didn’t get that part. Something about some contract being complicated so the witch chose to let them go?!<br><br>I just got so sick of this book after reading 50% of it. The MC needed to kill the princess <b>so she can save the kingdom. But why?!</b> She kept saying how she doesn’t want to do it, because she and the princess were best friends. <b> What I’d like to know is why killing the princess equals saving the kingdom.</b> And saving it from what anyway?! At 50%, after Kyra saying <i>''How much time before it was too late to save the princess and save the kingdom?''</i>, which she kept repeating and repeating throughout the story, I got f_ _ _ _ _ _ frustrated and run out of patience. <b>I have my limits of patience and this book crossed it.</b> Can someone enlighten me? Have I missed some clue/element which makes the idea of killing the princess the right thing to do or gives it a reason? <u>It's good to have some mystery in a book, but we also need some things to feed our curiosity with.</u><br><br>The romance was cute but OH SO CHEESY.<br><br><i>When Fred had come back without the witch socks the night before, she'd pretended to be sleeping. She felt him lie down beside her and could have sworn he was watchin her in the dark of the hayloft. Kyra hadn't dared risk opening her eyes to see. His breath fluttered against her face, and she felt the lightest touch on her cheek--something soft and warm resting there for the briefest second.<br><br>Fred had kissed her.</i><br><br><b>First of all, they met one or two days before this scene. Second of all, there wasn't even an insta-love!</b><br><br>Another thing that annoyed me was the fact that the characters were talking way too much in a 'modern' way when this book didn't feel that modern. I mean goblins being modern? LOL.<br><br>Like:<br><br><i>''I've heard of Seers,'' Fred went on, pulling a carrot out and taking a big bite. ''But I've never actually met one. It sounds pretty cool. Do you see the future?''</i><br><br>So... this book?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380425768ra/850019.gif" width="500" height="234" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>NOT RECOMMENDED! Or maybe for people with a lot of patience?<br><br><br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="4486768637247823048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_447339508" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/447339508" />
    <a title="Experiment BL626" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626"><img alt="Experiment BL626" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1335917426p2/4582872.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/447339508?book_show_action=true">Nov 02, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Experiment BL626" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Experiment BL626" href="/user/show/4582872-experiment-bl626">Experiment BL626</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4582872-experiment-bl626?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer447339508" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9009121682193321685"><i>Poison</i> delivered on its promise. It delivered a kickass heroine, a charming love interest, a cute pet pig, and an exciting plot. I devoured the book in less than 3 hours.<br/><br/><b>+ the characters</b><br/><br/>Kyra was everything I hope for in a heroine. She was resourceful, quick thinking, resilient, determined, selfless, noble, kind, etc. She deserved all the superlatives. I liked how she didn’t hesitate to kick ass, I liked that she fought smart, and even better I liked that she won most of the times. I liked how sh</span>
  <span id="freeText9009121682193321685" style="display:none"><i>Poison</i> delivered on its promise. It delivered a kickass heroine, a charming love interest, a cute pet pig, and an exciting plot. I devoured the book in less than 3 hours.<br /><br /><b>+ the characters</b><br /><br />Kyra was everything I hope for in a heroine. She was resourceful, quick thinking, resilient, determined, selfless, noble, kind, etc. She deserved all the superlatives. I liked how she didn’t hesitate to kick ass, I liked that she fought smart, and even better I liked that she won most of the times. I liked how she knew when to not fight but hide instead; I liked that she recognized her own limits. I liked how she came to adore her new pet pig, Rose. I liked how she eventually opened her heart to love, to Fred, in spite of the risks and her mission. The book constantly gave me reasons to love Kyra more. I was happy that the entire story was told in her 1st person POV so that I could receive her full awesomeness.<br /><br />Fred, the love interest, was charming, patient, and best of all nice. I thought YA had ruined me with its bad boy cliche because the few times I encountered good boy love interests I found them boring. I thought boys acting like jerks was the only way they, as love interests, could ever be interesting. Fred proved me wrong, and I was grateful for it. He proved that it was perfectly possible for a love interest to be both nice and interesting. I loved how patient he was with Kyra because Kyra didn’t have the time and couldn’t afford the time for romance. It would have been understandable if he was curt to her, but I was very glad he never was. Fred was seriously and thoroughly a nice boy.<br /><br />Rose, Kyra’s pet, was cute. She could have easily come off as annoying and a burden, but she didn’t.<br /><br /><b>+ the plot</b><br /><br />Even though there were flashbacks, one of which was particularly long, i.e. the entire chapter two, the pacing moved fast, and it was mainly due to the writing. The writing emphasized action and dialogue and painted imagery only when it was relevant. The plot always moved towards Kyra’s goal.<br /><br />I did not expect the amount of twists the plot had. Just when I thought the big twist was done and over, the plot pulled a few twists that were no less shocking. The ending pleased me.<br /><br /><b>+ negligible issues</b><br /><br />I did have a few issues with the book, but they were in the way of “this is good, but it could have slightly better.” I wished I learned more about the hermit, Ellie, and how he got into the conspiracy and what ultimately happened to him at the end of the story. It was easy to fill in the blanks but I preferred to know outright. Even though he was a bad guy, he was just so pitiful. <br /><br />Second issue was about Fred. I wanted to know how Fred got a wolf for a pet and learned how to steal like an experienced thief.<br /><br />Third issue was about the romance. I’m glad it wasn’t a love triangle, that Fred and Kyra mutually liked each other, and that the other girl was nice and not made out to be evil so she could be easily bumped off. However, I wished Kyra and Fred came together earlier and not at the very last minute. I wished they fought for each other and communicated with each other about how they really felt.<br /><br />Fourth issue was about the bad guy who was responsible for the main conflict. He was a caricature. The main conflict could have been avoided had the guy been disposed of in the first place when he got captured. In chapter 11, Kyra suggested people can be throw into prison for life for trivial reasons. If not executing him outright, he could have stayed in prison for life. On one hand, I’m glad the justice system had integrity. On the other hand, it seemed too good and simple to be real because what kingdom would willfully release a bad guy who will certainly return for vengeance. Anyway, once all was revealed and Kyra confronted him, he hit on her. WTF. <br /><br /><b>In Conclusion</b><br /><br />I rate <i>Poison</i> 4-stars for I really liked it. The book was fun and exciting. Both the plot and the protagonist were strong. While the book wasn’t without issues, I found them negligible. Frankly, the biggest issue I had was that the book was a standalone. I strongly felt there were more adventures in Kyra’s future to be told.<br /><br />If you like <i>Poison</i>, I recommend <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/6760761.The_False_Princess" title="The False Princess by Eilis O'Neal" rel="nofollow noopener">The False Princess</a>, which I rated 4-stars too.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9009121682193321685" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_464121013" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/464121013" />
    <a title="Jon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4277731-jon"><img alt="Jon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1384212540p2/4277731.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/464121013?book_show_action=true">Nov 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jon" href="/user/show/4277731-jon">Jon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=fairy-tales">fairy-tales</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4277731-jon?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer464121013" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13560739363871300603"> <a href='http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/03/poison-by-bridget-zinn-review-blog-tour.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seen at Scott Reads It!</a><br/> Poison is one of those books that I saw and I immediately wanted to read. Everything about the cover appealed to me from the "Snow White And The Huntsman" cover to the fantastic description. I never had the pleasure of meeting Bridget Zinn but I really wish I could have met her. From what I have heard and read online, Mrs. Zinn seemed like an amazing and humorous person! <br/> <br/> Kyra is on the run after a failed attempt at killing the Princess, who also is her best friend. Alo</span>
  <span id="freeText13560739363871300603" style="display:none"> <a href="http://scottreadsit.blogspot.com/2013/03/poison-by-bridget-zinn-review-blog-tour.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Seen at Scott Reads It!</a><br /> Poison is one of those books that I saw and I immediately wanted to read. Everything about the cover appealed to me from the "Snow White And The Huntsman" cover to the fantastic description. I never had the pleasure of meeting Bridget Zinn but I really wish I could have met her. From what I have heard and read online, Mrs. Zinn seemed like an amazing and humorous person! <br /> <br /> Kyra is on the run after a failed attempt at killing the Princess, who also is her best friend. Along the way on her journey Kyra meets Fred who is both charming and a bit arrogant. Will a bunch of potions and a pig be enough to find the Princess and kill her? Will Kyra manage to evade the army that's searching for her? Why did Kyra try to kill her best friend?<br /><br /><br /> Poison is by far one of the best fantasy books I have ever read! Bridget Zinn's debut is an extremely fun and entertaining read that is action-packed and filled with humor! This is an extremely addicting book that once you start, you won't be able to put it down! I love how even though this book revolves around an attempted murder, it is still a light and fun read.<br /><br /> The characters in Poison aren't exactly your average YA characters. Kyra was a character that I rooted for early on, even when she attempts to kill her best friend. I honestly never thought making potions could be so awesome and kick-ass until I read Poison. Kyra's potion abilities were incredible and they were extremely interesting to read about. Finally I have read about an extremely intelligent and witty character that was extremely likeable! Now a days in Young Adult literature, I seriously think a majority of the characters seem to lack a brain or common sense.<br /><br /> I'm super glad that Kyra didn't go all heads-over-heals for Fred. I have read so many books where the female protagonist claims she doesn't need a male to support her, and she falls immediately for the love interest. Fred, the love interest was named after the famous Fred Weasley from Harry Potter. Fred (from Poison) was extremely loyal to Kyra no matter what. I could definitely tell that Fred loved Kyra for who she was as a person. Even when Kyra abandons him for his good, Fred was persistent and kept coming back to her. Fred isn't one of those creepy stalker boyfriends that are rampant in almost every book I read. Kudos to Bridget Zinn for creating a likeable, charming love interest.<br /><br /> Everyone's probably wondering about Kyra's relationship with her love interest but frankly I'd rather discuss her relationship with her pig. Yes Kyra has a pig and her name is Rosie. The last time I loved a pig this much was when I first read Charlotte's Web. Rosie was seriously one of the most awesome animals I have ever read about it in a book (Sorry Rosie but I love Manchee and Wilbur more!). Though Kyra didn't always show it, I could tell she really loved Rosie.<br /><br /> I really enjoyed Poison and I would highly recommend it! Fans of Graceling will love Kyra and will love reading about her journey to kill the princess. Poison is definitely a must read with extremely likeable characters, fast paced action scenes, and tons of humor. Poison is an epic adventure unlike no other! Thank you to Disney-Hyperion for providing me with an ARC of Poison!<br /></span>

<div id="review_339253393" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/339253393" />
    <a title="Christina (Reading Extensively)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3471781-christina-reading-extensively"><img alt="Christina (Reading Extensively)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1269220159p2/3471781.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/339253393?book_show_action=true">May 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina (Reading Extensively)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina (Reading Extensively)" href="/user/show/3471781-christina-reading-extensively">Christina (Reading Extensively)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471781-christina-reading-extensively?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471781-christina-reading-extensively?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3471781-christina-reading-extensively?shelf=read2013">read2013</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer339253393" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8266092662002614266">I wasn't sure what to expect with this book but I was surprised by how much I enjoyed it. There is quite a bit of humor and lightheartedness so even though Kyra is on the run and has a dark task ahead of her, the story is actually fun. <br/><br/>Kyra is a smart and funny main character and she isn't perfect. She makes mistakes and sometimes trusts the wrong people or doesn't trust the right ones. I think this made her easier to relate to. There are some mysteries about her and some things that I wish were</span>
  <span id="freeText8266092662002614266" style="display:none">I wasn't sure what to expect with this book but I was surprised by how much I enjoyed it. There is quite a bit of humor and lightheartedness so even though Kyra is on the run and has a dark task ahead of her, the story is actually fun. <br /><br />Kyra is a smart and funny main character and she isn't perfect. She makes mistakes and sometimes trusts the wrong people or doesn't trust the right ones. I think this made her easier to relate to. There are some mysteries about her and some things that I wish were explored more such as her other abilities aside from potion making.<br /><br />Fred also adds to the humor and I love their banter. He is not exactly a "Prince Charming" type but he is a decent guy who still has the ability to make Kyra a bit weak-kneed at times (though she really fights the attraction-she has a job to do!). Instead of being a hero who saved the day, they really helped each other quite a bit.<br /><br />I do wish we'd gotten to know the secondary characters a little better. Of those characters, I think Princess Ariana is the one I felt I knew the best by the end of the book. Being able to see the flashbacks of their friendship through Kyra's memories certainly helped.<br /><br />The magical world that the author created was very interesting. I liked learning about how magic worked and the various potions Kyra could create. That aspect of the book reminded me of Princess Ben by Catherine Gilbert Murdock and I think Poison would appeal to fans of that book.<br /><br />Overall, although it had some minor flaws, I thought this book was charming and funny with some suspense and plot twists but nothing overly dark. Although this isn't a fairy tale, it has that kind of tone as well as light fantasy. I laughed out loud while reading and had a smile on my face as I turned the last page. I only wish there was more.<br /><br /><br />Note: I am honored that I had the opportunity to read an e-ARC of this book. It is so sad that the author Bridget Zinn did not live to see it published.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8266092662002614266" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/549416707?book_show_action=true">Mar 01, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hallie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hallie" href="/user/show/1145657-hallie">Hallie</a>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1145657-hallie?shelf=ya">ya</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer549416707" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer10801617339955835730">I decided not to rate this one, given the difficulty I was having knowing how to choose stars. There was a lot that was very sweet and enjoyable about the book, but Zinn's death before the book was even published may have had a lot to do with the unevenness I found. <br/><br/>Structurally, I think there was a serious problem with starting the book with the Bang! of knowing that Kyra had tried and failed to kill Princess Ariana (only daughter of the king and queen of the country). It's quite a while into t</span>
  <span id="freeText10801617339955835730" style="display:none">I decided not to rate this one, given the difficulty I was having knowing how to choose stars. There was a lot that was very sweet and enjoyable about the book, but Zinn's death before the book was even published may have had a lot to do with the unevenness I found. <br /><br />Structurally, I think there was a serious problem with starting the book with the Bang! of knowing that Kyra had tried and failed to kill Princess Ariana (only daughter of the king and queen of the country). It's quite a while into the book before we start to understand her reasoning, and a while more before we learn something crucial about the magic in the world further explaining that reasoning, and this lack of understanding makes investing in Kyra as a protagonist about whom we care very difficult. Aside from that, she's not just a skilled potions expert (in the case of Ariana, AKA assassin), she's a potions <i>master</i>. At sixteen. And she's not only learned everything she needs to know about potions (presumably from her teachers), but in the past she has been the potioner to administer an extremely tricky truth serum to a dangerous criminal, in a trial that will result in either his death or his freedom. (None of her teachers around to handle that job? Because Kyra didn't.)<br /><br />For all that, I enjoyed this book for the most part, and very much liked many of the characters - especially the pig, who outcuted even the dog. Obviously the tragedy is that Bridget Zinn died so young, leaving family and friends bereft, but a small part of the sadness is that she'd undoubtedly otherwise have written many more books that would have delighted many readers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10801617339955835730" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Michaels" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Michaels" href="/user/show/3601172-emma-michaels">Emma Michaels</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15950691307187435034">I am enamored with ‘Poison’. <br/><br/>I haven’t felt so wonderful reading a novel in ages. Finally twists I don’t see coming, adventure that swept me off my feet and a girl as stubborn and pig headed as I am. How could I not fall in love? Plus, did I mention there is a pig in this, poison throwing darts, crazy witches and royalty? I kid you not, no matter what is released later this year, this book will be my most beloved novel of 2013. Rosie <br/><br/>Have you ever read a book that brings back that first sense of</span>
  <span id="freeText15950691307187435034" style="display:none">I am enamored with ‘Poison’. <br /><br />I haven’t felt so wonderful reading a novel in ages. Finally twists I don’t see coming, adventure that swept me off my feet and a girl as stubborn and pig headed as I am. How could I not fall in love? Plus, did I mention there is a pig in this, poison throwing darts, crazy witches and royalty? I kid you not, no matter what is released later this year, this book will be my most beloved novel of 2013. Rosie <br /><br />Have you ever read a book that brings back that first sense of adventure you had when you started reading? This did that for me. I was swept off my feet and by the time I looked back up again hours had passed. I am a huge fan of ‘literary Easter eggs’ as plot tools and this book was bubbling to the brim with them, Bridget Zinn really knows how to write.<br /><br />Yes, to all of you readers who are fed up with series- <br /><br />This is a stand alone novel. <br /><br />One that actually ties up all of the lose ends into a magnificent bow at the end leaving you feeling like you just just read the most fulfilling novel and adventure you can imagine. I absolutely fell in love with this novel.<br /><br />You know those review that say, everything you want in a book you will find in __________. <br /><br />Yeah, in this case it is actually true. <br /><br />Adventure, romance, humor, fantastic characters who show real growth, excellent pacing, non-stop action but with attention to details and world building and a story you won’t forget. <br /><br />I may be addicted to e-books but I am definitely going out and getting a hardback copy of this book to keep on my desk right next to ‘The Fault in our Stars’ to remind me why I write.<br /><br />Poison is simply prefect.<br /></span>

<div id="review_509811988" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/509811988" />
    <a title="papalbina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4127748-papalbina"><img alt="papalbina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1575983753p2/4127748.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/509811988?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="papalbina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="papalbina" href="/user/show/4127748-papalbina">papalbina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4127748-papalbina?shelf=kindle-or-kobo-or-ipad">kindle-or-kobo-or-ipad</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4127748-papalbina?shelf=in-english">in-english</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4127748-papalbina?shelf=arc">arc</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4127748-papalbina?shelf=i-luv-that-cover">i-luv-that-cover</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer509811988" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15394306443606150803">When I was reading this book, I found out that Bridget Zinn died before she could see her novel published. That fact unsettled me because, among other things, Bridget and I were born in the same year, we were almost the same age when she passed away, and that remembers me (again) how brief our lives can be. <br/><br/>Although I think it's great that the book could be published in spite of everything, I really really think too that there was a lot of editing work missing in it that could have made the book</span>
  <span id="freeText15394306443606150803" style="display:none">When I was reading this book, I found out that Bridget Zinn died before she could see her novel published. That fact unsettled me because, among other things, Bridget and I were born in the same year, we were almost the same age when she passed away, and that remembers me (again) how brief our lives can be. <br /><br />Although I think it's great that the book could be published in spite of everything, I really really think too that there was a lot of editing work missing in it that could have made the book stand out instead of being just one among many. <br /><br />Some parts that affected the rhythm badly should have been cut out, some reasonable changes in the characters would have made them more believable, the embedding of some flash-backs was not timed right or the flash-back could have been spared, some scenes were too obvious where they were heading (like the river crossing part, I mean)... Don't get me wrong, I enjoyed reading the book, but I couldn't help seeing the flaws. <br /><br />But let me tell you the positive things of this book that makes me even sadder thinking that Bridget Zinn won't be writing stories like this one anymore:<br /><br />- Rosie, the piglet. That is a new approach to the animal companion and I liked it xDD And she was adorable. <br /><br />- Fred: I love his personality and the surprises he hid.<br /><br />- The other surprises, including the bad guy (yes, it surprised me, so what?), Kyra's secrets and unknown allies. <br /><br />- The potions, although I would have loved to have more details about them, but that's just my inner potioner :P<br /><br />- The book is very... hmmm... movie-ish? movie-able? movie-turnable? Don't know the word (if there is any). I could see it turned into a movie as enjoyable as "Ella Enchanted", for example. It has everything to be a great fantasy movie: potions, poisons, hidden talents, charismatic hero, strong heroine, princesses in distress, conspiracies, road trip... a piglet!!! It may not be the best written and structured book, but I think it could do a pretty good job as a story on the screen. It would make me very happy to watch that movie... <br /><br />In the end, the book is enjoyable and entertaining. Not the best one out there, but good enough to spend a couple of hours in it... <br /><br /><i>Thank you to Disney-Hyperion and netGalley for providing me with a copy of the book</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="15394306443606150803" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_433295905" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/433295905" />
    <a title="Lili" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9817760-lili"><img alt="Lili" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1426967124p2/9817760.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/433295905?book_show_action=true">Oct 13, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Lili" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Lili" href="/user/show/9817760-lili">Lili</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/9817760-lili?shelf=favorites-2012">favorites-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer433295905" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14277979523945049801"> Love. Love. Love. Love. LOVEEEEEEEEE. There are no other words to describe my feelings toward this story. Zinn managed to captivate me and take me on a really great adventure in a mere 276 pages. This is one of those books that you can't put down because not only is it adorable, it's simply perfect and leaves you aching for more of the author's easy skill of transporting you to new worlds. It kills me to realize that I won't be able to immerse myself in any other faraway lands that spur from Zi</span>
  <span id="freeText14277979523945049801" style="display:none"> Love. Love. Love. Love. LOVEEEEEEEEE. There are no other words to describe my feelings toward this story. Zinn managed to captivate me and take me on a really great adventure in a mere 276 pages. This is one of those books that you can't put down because not only is it adorable, it's simply perfect and leaves you aching for more of the author's easy skill of transporting you to new worlds. It kills me to realize that I won't be able to immerse myself in any other faraway lands that spur from Zinn's mind. Instead, I'm still fully content with re-reading my new pick-me-up fantasy.<br /><br /> <b> A RECIPE FOR POISON<br /> Ingredients:<br /><br /> Magical kingdom in peril<br /> Potions master (flavor: feisty)<br /> Evil princess (distilled from former best frien)<br /> Tiny pig (with essence of adorable)<br /> Handsome ruffian (must be funny, charming, good at rescuing; best if smells nice)<br /><br /> Blend with romance, add a dash of enchantment, mix well for mayhem and drizzle in humor.<br /> WARNING: Contents may be irresistible.</b><br /><br />That cute little description taken off of the back of my ARC describes this novel perfectly. An irresistibly enchanting tale with tons of laugh-out-loud humor, a perfect love interest, and the cutest little magical pig that you will ever encounter combines to form a tale of friendship and heroism that is remarkably perfect for all age groups. The young ones can find a really lovely tale and role model in Kyra while elder teens, like myself, can immerse themselves in a cute story that'll easily put a smile on their face a thousand times over.<br /><br />The plot of this novel was obviously fast-moving due to its short length, but I never felt rushed. It was full of magical creatures that I've never encountered before, as well as scary witches that eat people (think Hansel and Gretel's story but more physically revolting) and gypsies that just want to lend a hand. The wide array of creatures and characters easily allowed us to continuously be surprised, though the overarching finale of the story could be inferred by any reader able to read between the lines.<br /><br />But the most interesting aspect of the plot was clearly Kyra's Master Potioner status. There are only three masters in her kingdom and she is one of them. She can create potions that nobody ever dreamed of and loved her potion entitled Doze that puts people to sleep. Her darts tend to get her out of a lot of shady situations because of that little potion. But she does have one potion that can never fall into the wrong hands. It's got a red skull on it and it's entitled Poison...otherwise the only potion that can be used for immediate murder. The potion she used on her best friend, the Princess, out of fear that her marriage was going to cause her kingdom to fall. Would you be able to kill your best friend if it saved the entire kingdom? That's the question that led Kyra on the ultimate quest in this novel, and it's one that easily keeps you reading.<br /><br />Lastly, I want to address the characterization. Clearly, I am a huge fan of Kyra. She's amazingly strong-willed and determined. She's focused and brave and all around amazing. She's the type of heroine that should be written about more often because she can easily serve as a role-model to younger children. And then there's Fred. Gosh, I truly loved Fred. He's handsome, hilarious, and full of surprises. Most of the humor in this novel was delivered through him and his actions were often very surprising. And I must throw out a shout out to Langley the amazing wolf dog and his best friend/animal love Rosie the magical pig (who is the most adorable pig you will ever encounter, I tell you!)<br /><br />Needless to say, I have nothing but praise for this novel. I loved it more than I thought I would. What I originally imagined to be a cute read was not only adorable, but mesmerizing. Zinn is a literary genius and easily created a debut tale that is unforgettable. This story is not one to be missed. A must read for anyone of any age, even those who are not fantasy lovers.</span>
  <a data-text-id="14277979523945049801" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

The story started out strong and then lagged in the middle for me. By mid book it was a 3 star read but thankfully it finished with some fun twists at the end leaving me satisfied.   <span id="freeText5582027590470036105" style="display:none">Poison was a fun read that will likely appeal to a wide audience. It's appropriate for tweens and has appeal for older readers too. The story started out strong and then lagged in the middle for me. By mid book it was a 3 star read but thankfully it finished with some fun twists at the end leaving me satisfied. So glad I kept reading. I love when an element of the story takes me by surprise and this book did that for me. (In hindsight I guess I should have seen it coming but I love when I don't see something until it's there). <br /><br />There are some really fun elements to this story including an enchanted pig and a stranger named Fred who Kyra just can't seem to shake. I'll be passing this on to my daughter as I think she'll enjoy it.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Rating: 4 Stars - Great Book<br /><br />Content: Clean<br /><br />Source: Netgalley<br /><br />Genre/Reading Level: Young Adult fantasy appropriate for tweens on up.<br /><br /><br /><br /><br />Finished December 26, 2012<br /><br />*While visiting the author's website I just learned she passed away in 2011. <span id="freeTextContainer14283631278956237630">Yayyyyyy! I am SO glad that Debby forced me to read this book. Though I think it was on my to-read list anyway, I’m not certain I would ever have found the time to get to it, because there are an absurd number of books on my to-read shelf and I ALSO love rereading. I actually remember when this book was coming up, because I kept adding and removing it from my to-read shelf, because the reviews were ALL over the place, and I kept being convinced one way and then another, like a giant tug of war. </span>
  <span id="freeText14283631278956237630" style="display:none">Yayyyyyy! I am SO glad that Debby forced me to read this book. Though I think it was on my to-read list anyway, I’m not certain I would ever have found the time to get to it, because there are an absurd number of books on my to-read shelf and I ALSO love rereading. I actually remember when this book was coming up, because I kept adding and removing it from my to-read shelf, because the reviews were ALL over the place, and I kept being convinced one way and then another, like a giant tug of war. The winner of that tug of war was Debby. *doffs hat to Debby*<br /><br />Though I truly delighted in every page of Poison, I can see where it might not be everybody’s cup of cocoa. It’s all going to depend on your expectations and what you’re into. Thankfully, I went in with fairly low expectations and a feeling that the book would be flufftastic. It IS. There is NOTHING wrong with some well done fluff, and I had a big grin on my face the whole way through, so what is better than that?<br /><br />Read the <a href="http://readeroffictions.com/2014/02/sadie-hawkins-sunday-review-57-poison/" rel="nofollow noopener">full review</a> at <a href="http://readeroffictions.com" rel="nofollow noopener">A Reader of Fictions</a>.</span>

<div id="review_400479248" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/400479248" />
    <a title="Hypatia" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6608800-hypatia"><img alt="Hypatia" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1506843761p2/6608800.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/400479248?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Hypatia" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Hypatia" href="/user/show/6608800-hypatia">Hypatia</a>
      </span>

        rated it

<div id="review_565192170" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/565192170" />
    <a title="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah"><img alt="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1600525490p2/5701086.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/565192170?book_show_action=true">Mar 19, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*" href="/user/show/5701086-branwen-sedai-of-the-brown-ajah">Branwen Sedai *of the Brown Ajah*</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer565192170" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4791049110304354277">I want to talk about something first before I get into the actual review of this book. If you don't care to read it, feel free to skip to the next paragraph. But reading this book really made me realize some things (about myself particularly) that I really wanted to share with you guys. I promise its relevant (sort of). I've always loved to read. When I was a kid I read Little House on the Prairie and Goosebumps and stuff like that, but during the summer before I started high school I started lo</span>
  <span id="freeText4791049110304354277" style="display:none">I want to talk about something first before I get into the actual review of this book. If you don't care to read it, feel free to skip to the next paragraph. But reading this book really made me realize some things (about myself particularly) that I really wanted to share with you guys. I promise its relevant (sort of). I've always loved to read. When I was a kid I read Little House on the Prairie and Goosebumps and stuff like that, but during the summer before I started high school I started looking at books in a different way. I discovered V.C. Andrews and Dean Koontz and Stephen King and Brian Jacques and countless others. I went to the library every week, sometimes twice a week and just devoured the hell out of whatever I could get my hands on. I was never really a very social person, I always sort of preferred books (and animals) to people. But during that summer I had my first thought of, 'I wonder if I could write a book myself?' I realized that I wanted to make people feel good...the same way I felt when I read a book I really connected with. It was a desire that, once sparked, has never really left me. And I have a few novels that I've <br />been working on, that I've been dreaming of finishing and....life seemed to just keep getting in the way. I work six days a week, ten sometimes eleven hours a day, and I go to school at nights. And lots of times I want to sit down and work more on my book I say to myself, 'Not right now, I'm too tired,' or 'I can work on it later.' Not to say that I don't EVER work on it, I do write a little bit at least once a day, but there's always more I could be doing, you know? But you know what I have come to understand? There might not be a later. Bridget Zinn has taught me this. When I read about what happened to her, it broke my heart. Not just for her, but for myself. Bridget was a young woman who loved books and writing, yet she succumbed to illness before seeing her book published. And while I am so happy and thankful that it DID get published, it breaks my heart to know she never saw it happen. It really made me understand how short life is. No one knows how much time we each have left. And we have to make the most of what we do have. Dream huge. Live even huger. Do everything you thought you would never do. Push until you make every wish come true. For me, that means getting my ass in the chair and working on finishing my book(s), no matter how fucking tired I may be, or how hard it may get. Take all the ideas swirling inside my head and turn them into characters and scenarios that will (hopefully) make other people smile and be happy. Because it's my dream. And I don't want to ever give it up. And I honestly can't imagine any other way I want to spend my life than writing and reading. So Bridget, wherever you are, I just want to thank you for writing this amazing book, even if you didn't get to see it published. And thank you for your passion and your dream and your determination to see it though. You've really helped me to understand just how precious life is. <br /><br />That being said, now on to the actual book review! :) This book was seriously amazing! It was such a perfect, light, fun, fantasy story. I didn't want to stop reading it because it was so wonderful, but at the same time I couldn't keep myself from devouring it as quickly as possible because I couldn't wait to find out what happened next. There were a few twists and turns toward the end that I did NOT see coming, and it was super fun to be surprised with that. And also theres a sweet little pig named Rosie...A PIG NAMED ROSIE HOW EFFING CUTE IS THAT!?!?! *sighs happily* This book was great. If you love fantasy (espesically fantasy with humor in it) you will no doubt adore this book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4791049110304354277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_568766500" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/568766500" />
    <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers"><img alt="TheBookSmugglers" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1316717753p2/1223249.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/568766500?book_show_action=true">Mar 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheBookSmugglers" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheBookSmugglers" href="/user/show/1223249-thebooksmugglers">TheBookSmugglers</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1223249-thebooksmugglers?shelf=fluff">fluff</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer568766500" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1802216735835126519">Originally reviewed on <a href='http://thebooksmugglers.com/2013/04/book-review-poison-by-bridget-zinn.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Book Smugglers</a><br/><br/>At just sixteen years old, Kyra is one of the most powerful and celebrated figures in the kingdom - one of the Master Trio of Potioners with exceptional talent, Kyra is also the best friend of Princess Ariana, who just so happens to be the direct heir and future ruler of the land. But one day, Kyra does the unthinkable: she attempts to kill her best friend by way of poisoned blade, and misses.<br/><br/>Now Kyra has fallen from upstanding member of society to villai</span>
  <span id="freeText1802216735835126519" style="display:none">Originally reviewed on <a href="http://thebooksmugglers.com/2013/04/book-review-poison-by-bridget-zinn.html" rel="nofollow noopener">The Book Smugglers</a><br /><br />At just sixteen years old, Kyra is one of the most powerful and celebrated figures in the kingdom - one of the Master Trio of Potioners with exceptional talent, Kyra is also the best friend of Princess Ariana, who just so happens to be the direct heir and future ruler of the land. But one day, Kyra does the unthinkable: she attempts to kill her best friend by way of poisoned blade, and misses.<br /><br />Now Kyra has fallen from upstanding member of society to villain, and she takes to the road, trying to stay ahead of the royal guard as well as tangling with other dangers that face a girl on the run (goblins, thieves, witches, handsome and charismatic traveling companions, etc). Though she's on the outs right now, Kyra is single-mindedly dedicated to her mission to find and kill Princess Ariana - the future of the kingdom depends on it. Luckily, she has the help of an adorable, magical scent-seeking pig (named Rosie) and one handsome and charismatic traveling companion (named Fred) and his wolfish dog to help her on her mission. <br /><br />The debut (and sadly, last) novel from Bridget Zinn, <em>Poison</em> has a killer premise: smarmy and talented girl goes rogue and repeatedly tries to find and assassinate her best friend for specific reasons unknown.* Surprisingly, given the novel's core premise, the book <em>isn't</em> all doom and gloom; rather, <em>Poison</em> is a diverting, frothy romp of a fantasy novel. Written in a contemporary voice and featuring a snarky, strong female protagonist, this book feels and sounds very much like a fantastical Meg Cabot book (as many other reviews have pointed out before me). And, like Meg Cabot's books, <em>Poison</em> will certainly appeal to many readers - particularly those looking for some wit, lighthearted banter, and a sweet romance. <br /><br />From a plotting perspective, <em>Poison</em> also does a fine job, creating a captivating mystery and chase story, as readers wonder <em>why</em> Kyra is so dead-set on killing the Princess - the reveal is solid, too (although the end of the book feels a little unresolved). On the whole, the romantic angle is of the instant variety, but sweet, the characters and world also of the fresh-faced, Pretty-Prince-and-Princess (of the western European) mold. And there IS an adorable magical pig who plays a main part in the story. Cute. Right?<br /><br />These praises said, however, this is not exactly a deep or meaningful book - and the comparisons to the meatier works of Tamora Pierce or Kristin Cashore are, in this reviewer's opinion, way off base. Heck, even in comparison to some of the more lighthearted YA/MG fantasy novels - my favorite Patricia C. Wrede's Enchanted Forest books immediately come to mind - <em>Poison</em> can't quite stack up. The contemporary voice is intensely off-putting, and the haphazard, imagined magical rules and power structures (even at a very basic level) is frustrating. And yet, for those criticisms, I can't really fault the book because it is exactly what it presents itself as: fun, silly, with all the sweetness and airiness of strawberry shortcake. <br /><br />Which is to say, it won't fill you up, but if you're in the mood for shortcake, you can't go wrong with <em>Poison</em>.<br /><br />----------<br />*Sadly, Bridget Zinn passed away before the publication of this book, to cancer. You can read more about Bridget and her work <a href="http://www.bridgetzinn.com/about_bridget/index.php" rel="nofollow noopener">here</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1802216735835126519" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
